  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c6c1759c-510c-495f-b635-31b997389e72'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

She struggles for survival and for self-esteem, embarking on a love affair with the 18-year-old son of her most powerful opponent, brutal and charismatic rancher, Buck Calder.</span>

<div id="review_46138979" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46138979" />
    <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books"><img alt="Allison (The Allure of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1247775031p2/1637878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46138979?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison (The Allure of Books)" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books">Allison (The Allure of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440224624" href="/book/show/828173.The_Loop">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Allison (The Allure of Books) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1530627-jeane">Jeane</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46138979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9634434537588527770">This has been recommended to me by several friends here on GR, and while I trust their judgment...I still didn't expect to fall in love with this story as quickly as I did. Before the plot gets going, Evans introduces you to a cast of rich and varied characters that are alone worth reading the book for. I was so caught up in their lives that before I knew it I was surrounded by a plot of wolves and intrigue! <br/><br/>The story was so realistic, there was quite a bit of detail of how the wolves live, how </span>
  <span id="freeText9634434537588527770" style="display:none">This has been recommended to me by several friends here on GR, and while I trust their judgment...I still didn't expect to fall in love with this story as quickly as I did. Before the plot gets going, Evans introduces you to a cast of rich and varied characters that are alone worth reading the book for. I was so caught up in their lives that before I knew it I was surrounded by a plot of wolves and intrigue! <br /><br />The story was so realistic, there was quite a bit of detail of how the wolves live, how the various Wildlife crew members and biologists studied them, and also weaved through the story were stories about how they had been hunted and trapped for over 100 years in Hope, the city in which the story takes place.<br /><br />I recommend this very highly...it was at times gut-wrenching, beautiful, terrible and heroic. This was my first Evans, but it won't be my last!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9634434537588527770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1979017520245032129">How do you write the review of such a nice book? Perhaps, by not saying too much about it and just letting all its sacred moments regurgitate in your mind.. This one is what I would call a perfect book to follow up on, if the only one of Evans you've read is the <i>Horse Whisperer</i>. <br/> The typical strong start that has been inherent in Nicholas Evans writings since Horse Whisperer (and we all hope he doesn't change that, I love the way he begins) is present in The Loop too. The book never loses its fo</span>
  <span id="freeText1979017520245032129" style="display:none">How do you write the review of such a nice book? Perhaps, by not saying too much about it and just letting all its sacred moments regurgitate in your mind.. This one is what I would call a perfect book to follow up on, if the only one of Evans you've read is the <i>Horse Whisperer</i>. <br /> The typical strong start that has been inherent in Nicholas Evans writings since Horse Whisperer (and we all hope he doesn't change that, I love the way he begins) is present in The Loop too. The book never loses its focus and has been kept on a pretty tight leash, never wavering from the intensity that Evans generates initially. In fact, take my word for it, it only gets more complicated and intense; the human relationships and man's animal instincts becoming intertwined and keeping you moving from page to page. Do NOT miss any chance to read it. </span>

<div id="review_39286263" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39286263" />
    <a title="Fiona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1356469-fiona"><img alt="Fiona" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39286263?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona" href="/user/show/1356469-fiona">Fiona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fiona by: </span>
      Jeane, Atishay
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1356469-fiona?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1356469-fiona?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1356469-fiona?shelf=setting-usa">setting-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1356469-fiona?shelf=second-hand">second-hand</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39286263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14337832886464718420">Boy, am I glad I allowed myself to be persuaded to read this book. Although, persuade is a rather light description of the methods used to induce me to read The Loop. I forgive them though.<br/><br/>Thanks goes to Jeane, Atishay and Kathy who for many a long day campaigned for me to read this book and I can't blame them. <br/><br/>It was fantastic. <br/><br/>Nicholas Evans is one of those gold dust authors who has some magical ability to capture thoughts, feelings, actions, movements - everything in words without even trying</span>
  <span id="freeText14337832886464718420" style="display:none">Boy, am I glad I allowed myself to be persuaded to read this book. Although, persuade is a rather light description of the methods used to induce me to read The Loop. I forgive them though.<br /><br />Thanks goes to Jeane, Atishay and Kathy who for many a long day campaigned for me to read this book and I can't blame them. <br /><br />It was fantastic. <br /><br />Nicholas Evans is one of those gold dust authors who has some magical ability to capture thoughts, feelings, actions, movements - everything in words without even trying to, seemingly. <br /><br />The Loop grabs you by the throat and takes you on the most beautiful, suspenseful and exhilarating journey a book can give you. I was really worried all the way throughout - Evans held my heart at ransom I think, asking me want to finish this book, even though part of me was scared to, and part of me didn't ever want to leave the book.<br /><br />It was a difficult read. I love wolves, perhaps that is what put me off reading this book for a long time. I remember looking at it in the shop years ago, especially when I was about 14 wondering about it. I think at the time I wasn't ready or mature enough for such a book, but perhaps the reason why I did look at it in the shop a couple of times (it always seemed to be on sale in train stations funnily enough I remember) was because I knew deep down it was a book I'd read in the future. And now I have thanks to some gentle coercion. <br /><br />The Loop, is a book you immerse yourself in. When you open the book, you do not read you just feel and see and hear and smell. You are constantly on the edge of something. It is about survival, love and redemption. <br /><br />Once again, as in The Divide, Evans has given birth to real characters, people who inhabit your brain and who you can't stop thinking about. <br /><br />The Loop weaves a story of love, redemption, life and survival. When Helen comes to Hope, Montana, she is not at first hopeful of anything. Her love life is a mess and she is a born cynic. She comes to Montana to help protect a wolf pack who have recently been suspected of killing the rancher's cattle. Life for poor Helen though doesn't become any easier when she meets one of the most influential ranchers in Hope - a Buck Calder. <br /><br />For those of you who haven't read a Nicholas Evans yet, you're missing out. I can't wait to read his other two - but I am going to wait! The Brave is coming out later this year and maybe if I can eke the other two I have not read out over the year then I will not have to wait so long for his new book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14337832886464718420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_426633084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426633084" />
    <a title="Adam Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2377841-adam-nelson"><img alt="Adam Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501852p2/2377841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426633084?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Nelson" href="/user/show/2377841-adam-nelson">Adam Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426633084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9525158505718929147">What sweet joy Nicholas Evans is after putting myself through most of Jean Auel's "Earth's Children" series. I couldn't help but draw comparisons with The Plains of Passage as I read, although, to be fair, Auel and Evans are writing completely different stories for a different era. Still, there's romance, nature, hunting, and sex here, and Evans handles all with such grace and restraint where Auel will go on for 100 pages telling you how Ayla makes soup, and then another 100 pages with everyone </span>
  <span id="freeText9525158505718929147" style="display:none">What sweet joy Nicholas Evans is after putting myself through most of Jean Auel's "Earth's Children" series. I couldn't help but draw comparisons with The Plains of Passage as I read, although, to be fair, Auel and Evans are writing completely different stories for a different era. Still, there's romance, nature, hunting, and sex here, and Evans handles all with such grace and restraint where Auel will go on for 100 pages telling you how Ayla makes soup, and then another 100 pages with everyone telling her how amazing she is that she can make soup.<br /><br />Here, Evans has a few asides from the main plot to provide the compelling backstory that explains the book's title, and without doing it for you, he provides the basis for a metaphor that interlocks these characters, whether good or bad. And there are no REAL villains here. There is villainous behavior, but Evans cares, even about people who make decisions that you know he personally doesn't agree with. He doesn't judge his characters. He never does, not even Buck Calder. Even the simplest-seeming among them have a deep complexity that is informed by their circumstances and the dilemma of trying to raise cattle and ensure the safety of their children in a region inhabited by wild wolves. <br /><br />The wolves themselves are occasionally characters here. Evans describes their breeding, the way they live, the way they hunt and provide for their young, but again, I'm reminded of Auel and the mammoth porn that began Plains of Passage, and I'm thinking, Evans wants us to fall in love with his story in a way that makes sense to how the intelligent human psyche actually works. Less is more. Whereas Auel shows her mammoths peeing and pooping all over each other before sex and describes what it probably smelled and tasted like, then gives you the length and girth of the male mammoth's member, Evans knows that it destroys any rapports he has with his reader to expound like this. I just respect him so much for that. <br /><br />I wasn't sure I could be moved by The Loop as I had been by The Smoke Jumper. I had thought from the outset that Evans was trying to advocate for some environmentalist platform. I wouldn't hold it against him, but I can't be captivated by a political stance. Fortunately, he doesn't do that. Instead, actually, the ultra-conservative and ultra-liberal alike will be challenged to put politics on hold and just allow Evans to make you feel--for the wolves, for the ranchers (including Buck), for the wolfer, and for Helen Ross, the biologist and heroine of the novel. I was surprised to feel as moved as I did and thankful that I could so easily put my politics aside to be transported. Evans has a way--he just gets me. <br /><br />SPOILER ALERT (Diana, this especially means you. I'm serious.)<br /><br />I'm trying to be as vague as possible about the ending, but nevertheless, even hinting at the way the story turns out, however obliquely, requires a stern warning, so there you go. This book brought me to tears by its ending, and I've thought about it, about whether I was just manipulated by a superfluous happy ending or if it had a point beyond just making me insanely happy, and I think it did, which is why I feel confident in giving this five stars. Buck's grief is about hurting his son and tearing his family apart, but I also think there was something in him that grieved for the wolves he'd killed. He realized that he had damaged his own soul. It's not about the wolves but about the part of us that deliberately wants to kill, thinking that it's a noble gesture that will protect the ones we love, but we can become so obsessed that we will deliberately hurt the ones we love in order to do it. The wolves have an instinctual understanding of this delicate balance but we humans, being creatures of free-will, need to learn it, some more than others. I think Buck is grieved because he had to learn it the hard way, and he now finally realizes all that he has lost. He provided for his family, but he was never really present for them. He cheated on his wife, refused to acknowledge his son Luke, and, seeking to protect the cattle that had brought him so much fortune, broke federal laws to kill wolves whom he didn't even know for sure may have been killing his cattle. Evans doesn't spell that out for you, and I'm grateful. I'm glad to arrive at such a conclusion on my own.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9525158505718929147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_727351130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727351130" />
    <a title="Ian Allan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17308033-ian-allan"><img alt="Ian Allan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361684026p2/17308033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727351130?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Allan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Allan" href="/user/show/17308033-ian-allan">Ian Allan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727351130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2827528514714924251">I'm late to the party on Nicholas Evans. He had the mega-hit "Horse Whisperer" in 1995, but I didn't read it at that time. I didn't read anything of his until my wife brought "The Divide" home from the library. It's a masterpiece, and now I'm trying to work my way through his other books. He's really good. He's not a cookie-cutter type author like Cliver Cussler or James Patterson, who's cranking out a couple of books a year. He's carefully putting together epic, brilliant stories. Those take mo</span>
  <span id="freeText2827528514714924251" style="display:none">I'm late to the party on Nicholas Evans. He had the mega-hit "Horse Whisperer" in 1995, but I didn't read it at that time. I didn't read anything of his until my wife brought "The Divide" home from the library. It's a masterpiece, and now I'm trying to work my way through his other books. He's really good. He's not a cookie-cutter type author like Cliver Cussler or James Patterson, who's cranking out a couple of books a year. He's carefully putting together epic, brilliant stories. Those take more time. Like "The Divide", this one is based in Montana. (Why is an English guy writing books about this area? I have no idea). Quality is similar. He carefully develops a half dozen characters, and then pushes them around on the chessboard. Very satisfying. My wife tells me "The Brave" falls short of these two Evans books. I will move onto the Horse Whisperer next. I saw the movie, but it's been so long I don't even remember it. And with the amount they have to cut out of these books to squeeze them down into less than two hours, I'm sure there's all kinds of stuff that would have been left out anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2827528514714924251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_79152717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79152717" />
    <a title="Tara Chevrestt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2544368-tara-chevrestt"><img alt="Tara Chevrestt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399003936p2/2544368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79152717?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Chevrestt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Chevrestt" href="/user/show/2544368-tara-chevrestt">Tara Chevrestt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79152717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9762397978760758959">I loved this book so much I have read it twice. I related to Helen and even to young Luke. I sympathized with him and the abuse he suffers at his dad's hands. I also felt Helen's frustrations with the ranchers and the way they treated her or talked down to her. The look at the lives of wolves in Yellowstone and the tracking process was fascinating. I plan on reading this for a third time.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1299134025" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299134025" />
    <a title="Lily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1899725-lily"><img alt="Lily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451003929p2/1899725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299134025?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily" href="/user/show/1899725-lily">Lily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385317009" href="/book/show/227572.The_Loop">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=animals">animals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299134025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1234361020050703308">This book walks the line in an unusual way: the stretches of formulaic drama almost ruined my interest, but the tense action scenes and hints of moral introspection were just enough to keep me turning the pages. <br/><br/>The story unfolds in the town of Hope, Montana. In the nearby wilderness, a pack of reintroduced wolves - part of a government effort to restore wolf populations after they had been hunted to near extinction - are on the hunt. The trouble is, Hope is a community of cattle ranchers, and a</span>
  <span id="freeText1234361020050703308" style="display:none">This book walks the line in an unusual way: the stretches of formulaic drama almost ruined my interest, but the tense action scenes and hints of moral introspection were just enough to keep me turning the pages. <br /><br />The story unfolds in the town of Hope, Montana. In the nearby wilderness, a pack of reintroduced wolves - part of a government effort to restore wolf populations after they had been hunted to near extinction - are on the hunt. The trouble is, Hope is a community of cattle ranchers, and any threat to their livestock and livelihood is taken dead seriously. Into this fiercely self-sufficient little town comes Helen Ross: a wildlife biologist on a mission to track and protect the wolves, and to keep the locals' growing anger at bay. <br /><br />A few facts about Helen: <br /><br />1) She is enchantingly attractive and exerts a magnetic pull on every man she meets. <br />2) She is wholly unaware of point #1. <br />3) Her sense of self-worth hinges on her romantic relationships. <br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />Among the locals that Helen meets (and inevitably charms) are the powerful, charismatic, ruthless rancher Buck Calder, and his sensitive son Luke, who suffers from a speech impediment. To the chagrin of his father, Luke cares deeply about nature, including wolves. He sees in wild animals a reflection of himself: creatures struggling to cope with the way that humans run the world, and unable to speak up for themselves. Luke is probably the character that I found most interesting. <br /><br />Most of the characters, are introduced with several pages of backstory that tend to consist of difficult disappointments and/or sticky romantic entanglements. I found myself having to take in large tracts of information about characters that I didn't particular care about yet - I would rather have had my interest sparked, and then discover more about these people bit by bit. And perhaps some blanks are just better left unfilled. A bigger problem is that the use of so many big, external disasters in their histories - death, disease, betrayal - made it seem that these were the only things the characters were shaped by. Certainly, those big events can sculpt people's lives, but so can less obvious things, and I was left feeling that most people in the book were a little underdeveloped - despite all the time spent showing the hardships they'd been through. <br /><br />The overarching feeling was of channel-surfing through soap operas, occasionally interspersed with nature documentaries. <br /><br />However, I can say that when the author wanted to create tension and excitement, he did it very well. There were a bunch of scenes during which the pages flew by. There were also parts of the book (dealing with hunting and trapping) that I personally found too distressing to read carefully, which I ended up having to skim through. Not really a negative or a positive, just a matter of my own sensitivity.<br /><br />The book did stimulate my interest in the history of human interactions with wolves. While reading the descriptions of the early boom in wolf hunting, the word that came to mind was, simply, genocide. The fact that some people (over the course of generations, or sometimes over the course of a single life) have come to realize that killing off an entire species is a bad idea - and that it's worthwhile trying to do something to remedy it - made me feel a little bit more optimistic about how humans might interact with other species in the future. <br /><br /><i>Indian folklore had it that the spirits of all America's slaughtered wolves lived on... Awaiting a time when they might safely walk again upon the earth.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1234361020050703308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_252688110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252688110" />
    <a title="Michael Rullo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7207720-michael-rullo"><img alt="Michael Rullo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583618427p2/7207720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252688110?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Rullo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Rullo" href="/user/show/7207720-michael-rullo">Michael Rullo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440224624" href="/book/show/828173.The_Loop">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who loves wolves, romance enthusiasts</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michael by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5183533-brenda-knight">Brenda Knight</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7207720-michael-rullo?shelf=nature">nature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7207720-michael-rullo?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252688110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5405386066200665343">My mother suggested this book to me at a young age. She loved Evan's other book, The Horse Whisperer, and since she knew I love wolves, she had to get me this book. It was one of the best things my mother ever gave me. I still own a copy of it and anytime I don't have a good book to read, I'll always fall back on that one. The story is very solid, the grammar, mechanics, and plot all have sound bases, but that's not why you love a story, that's just what makes you able to love it. I connected wi</span>
  <span id="freeText5405386066200665343" style="display:none">My mother suggested this book to me at a young age. She loved Evan's other book, The Horse Whisperer, and since she knew I love wolves, she had to get me this book. It was one of the best things my mother ever gave me. I still own a copy of it and anytime I don't have a good book to read, I'll always fall back on that one. The story is very solid, the grammar, mechanics, and plot all have sound bases, but that's not why you love a story, that's just what makes you able to love it. I connected with this story very strongly as a young country boy who had acres of woods as his playground. I always loved nature, and had a strong connection with animals. We bred dogs throughout my childhood, and the wolf was the creature that connected my love for dogs to my love for the wild and for nature. While reading The Loop, I was carried away into the setting, I understood the main character's tainted perspective and unwillingness to trust due to my own troubled past. I will want to read this story again because I've lost so many of the details over the years, but I still cling to it with more than fond memories and hold it as a dear piece of my past. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5405386066200665343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_572512235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572512235" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/938229-david"><img alt="David" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/572512235?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/938229-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440224624" href="/book/show/828173.The_Loop">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer572512235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12973189949111293445">Sparks seems to truly understand small town life and the work involved in ranching. This time, he does for wolves what he did for horses in "The Horse Whisperer." Okay, not really, but he writes a compelling novel with building conflict between the biologists who want to protect the wolves and the ranchers who want them eradicated in order to protect their livestock. There is a long-standing hatred between the cattlemen and the wolves and an incident brings this conflict to a near war. Remember,</span>
  <span id="freeText12973189949111293445" style="display:none">Sparks seems to truly understand small town life and the work involved in ranching. This time, he does for wolves what he did for horses in "The Horse Whisperer." Okay, not really, but he writes a compelling novel with building conflict between the biologists who want to protect the wolves and the ranchers who want them eradicated in order to protect their livestock. There is a long-standing hatred between the cattlemen and the wolves and an incident brings this conflict to a near war. Remember, these ranchers carry rifles in their pickups. <br /><br />Along the way, we see the flaws in some characters-- Buck Calder, a well-to-do rancher, who is a womanizer, a smoozer, and an outspoken enemy of the wolves. Helen, the biologist brought in to track and monitor the wolves has her pain and struggle with self-worth gradually revealed to the reader. Luke Calder, the young adult son of Buck, who struggles with a stutter and a feeling of guilt over the death of his older brother. <br /><br />The author deals well with the small town mentality in these farm towns. He seems to understand the work involved in ranching and some of the problems that go along with it-- one section of the novel describes some of the breeding-- some of the switch from Herefords to Black Angus as a breed and the reasons.. how feeding schedule affects calving, etc. Really interesting stuff-- <br /><br />From time to time, the author ranges afar from the action and lounges around in cheap romantic drivel. In other words, there are moments when it is difficult to tell whether the novel is a romance novel with wolves thrown in or the other way around. The romantic stuff is alright, but there are moments when it gets in the way of a good story. <br /><br />The climax of the novel is a bit anti-climatic, with the author undoing a portion of the climax in the final chapter, trying to wrap it all up in a nice romantic package and trying to offer the reader a happy ending. Trying is indeed a good description... For the final conclusion is bittersweet for me-- having one character learn his lesson and the other characters continuing down a path that seemed built on sappy\puppy love.<br /><br />Still, it was a pretty good book and I enjoyed it.. the author seemed quite familiar with the elements he threw in, whether it was describing animals, breeds, wolves, trucks, traps, etc. It all seemed like he got the details all right. And that always helps a novel, even if it is just romantic drivel. {grin}</span>
  <a data-text-id="12973189949111293445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64194828" />
    <a title="Dena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1405313-dena"><img alt="Dena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417012272p2/1405313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64194828?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dena" href="/user/show/1405313-dena">Dena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer64194828&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64194828" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5365518754722882044">I enjoyed this book but was surprised that I didn't come away with a totally clear picture of what the author believed was the answer to wolf reintroduction. It was very clear at the beginning that the wolf "was thinking" about getting the baby vs. the cattle. And then throughout the book there was sympathy built for the wolves and the biologists because of the rash and selfish way that the ranchers approached everything. But I thought the secret release of the new alpha couple at the end was pr</span>
  <span id="freeText5365518754722882044" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book but was surprised that I didn't come away with a totally clear picture of what the author believed was the answer to wolf reintroduction. It was very clear at the beginning that the wolf "was thinking" about getting the baby vs. the cattle. And then throughout the book there was sympathy built for the wolves and the biologists because of the rash and selfish way that the ranchers approached everything. But I thought the secret release of the new alpha couple at the end was probably the author's true heart. I didn't agree with that. And I don't agree with not being able to shoot them when they are after the ranchers cattle. However, going after then with vengeance and hate isn't appropriate either..... Then there was the wolfer. His suicide after realizing that the wolves had that spark was interesting. But I'd be differing with that too. They are alive and should be treated with the respect that anything deserves as a creation of God. And that includes killing them humanely when necessary - not clandestinely.<br /><br />Anyway - it was a good story and I learned a lot about the program and these beautiful animals.</span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2647678628?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/76044072-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789022524084" href="/book/show/2352204.De_wolvenlus">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2647678628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15956544106715303035"><i>"What is it about those animals that people hate so much?" "About wolves? I don't know. Maybe they are too much like us. When we look at them, we see ourselves. Loving, caring, social beings who happen to be terrible murderers." Eleanor considered this. ''Maybe it also comes from jealousy.'' ''In what way?'' ''That they are still part of nature and that we don't how to do that anymore.''</i><br/><br/>Wow! I can't believe I only came across this book by incidence given the fact that <i>the Horse Whisperer</i> by Nich</span>
  <span id="freeText15956544106715303035" style="display:none"><i>"What is it about those animals that people hate so much?" "About wolves? I don't know. Maybe they are too much like us. When we look at them, we see ourselves. Loving, caring, social beings who happen to be terrible murderers." Eleanor considered this. ''Maybe it also comes from jealousy.'' ''In what way?'' ''That they are still part of nature and that we don't how to do that anymore.''</i><br /><br />Wow! I can't believe I only came across this book by incidence given the fact that <i>the Horse Whisperer</i> by Nicholas Evans used to be one of my childhood favorites. <br /><br /><i>The Loop</i> portrays a story world I love to live in. Mainly because of the beautiful descriptions of nature in the area of this sleepy fictional town Hope (Montana) in which the book is set. The story emphasizes strongly on man's connection with nature and how we all have a role to play in it. Although this book was written in 1998, I think Evans addresses some fundamental questions that are more relevant today than ever before. How do we shape the part we have to play as humans and are we truly able to distinguish right from wrong? <br /><br />The story revolves around the reappearance of wolves after a massive slaughter of these animals one and a half century ago. Now there is the law and the government to protect them, but ranchers are furious about the wolves killing their cattle and tempers flare. The reader becomes to understand the controversy that follows from reintroducing the wolf, and different perspectives on this topic are displayed fairly neutrally. This means that the writer does not judge his characters, even though you know he does not approve of all of their actions. The great strength of this book lies in the multiple interesting characters as well, I just could not stop reading about the ranchers and biologists and the ongoing dynamics between them in the small village of Hope. I'm amazed by all the character development Evans manages to write down in the space of one book, without ever straying too far from the plot line. He illustrates characters that are somewhat out of the ordinary but maybe this is exactly what makes them feel so outstandingly real. Luke and Eleanor Calder I liked best, each of them such strong and unique personalities. There even was fascinating and gripping romance about which I was curious to find out more. From time to time the story centers around the wolves as characters themselves, which is a valuable addition to the story and makes it all more emotional in my opinion. <br /><br />I absolutely loved this book. I'm positive I will be reading the other works of this author soon enough. This was such good storytelling.. nature, love, romance, morality, remorse and finally redemption, it was all in there. The ending left me vaguely wistful but it all tied together so beautifully, it sincerely couldn't have been done any better. The book really touched me and therefore I know this is one of those stories that will stay with me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15956544106715303035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_835870686" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/835870686" />
    <a title="Berke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13817386-berke"><img alt="Berke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376906519p2/13817386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/835870686?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Berke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berke" href="/user/show/13817386-berke">Berke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385317009" href="/book/show/227572.The_Loop">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13817386-berke?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer835870686&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer835870686" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11546639631986397225">'The Loop' by Nicholas Evans is a well paced book. There is a good amount of suspense and drama. Evans does a successful job of creating characters that you care about and feel for.<br/><br/>The story centers around a field biologist named Helen Ross, who has been sent a small town named Hope in-----. She is an enthusiastic, comical, diligent, amiable but defensive and fragile person. Because of her failed relationships she suffers from a mental storm but does her best to conceal it by occupying herself. </span>
  <span id="freeText11546639631986397225" style="display:none">'The Loop' by Nicholas Evans is a well paced book. There is a good amount of suspense and drama. Evans does a successful job of creating characters that you care about and feel for.<br /><br />The story centers around a field biologist named Helen Ross, who has been sent a small town named Hope in-----. She is an enthusiastic, comical, diligent, amiable but defensive and fragile person. Because of her failed relationships she suffers from a mental storm but does her best to conceal it by occupying herself. The main antagonist is Buck Calder, an influential, affluent, and crafty rancher who is highly respected in his town. He has a son named Luke who has a prominent role in the story. Buck is humiliated by him because Luke is a stutterer and different person than himself. Therefore he isolates Luke from the outer world and even within his family. Buck sees him as a personal failure. On top of this his he loathes Luke's bunny-hugger trait because Luke cares about the animals and nature around him. He does everything he can to protect it from his father and always refrains from killing cattle predators which is an unusual thing for a rancher.<br /><br />Luke isolates himself from reality into a world where he feels safe and accepted: nature. He finds refuge in his frequent forest visits to escape his father's scrutiny and disaproval. Luke is my favorite character. What I like the most is that from a silent recluse he becomes a mature and confidant man at the end of the book. This was very well thought and written. Evans is right too because sometimes people can be too judgmental thus leading stutterers like Luke to close up. Animals can be more comforting.<br /><br />The plot of the story is formed around a failing government wild life program that aims to protect wolves as an endangered species. The Hope ranchers have suffered many cattle casualties. This instigates unrest and leads to an open rebellion against the wolves at the end. So there is an overt conflict between the locals and law. <br /><br />Besides the plot and characters' personalities I thought that the relationships were realistic and consistent with the characters' demeanors. For example: Luke- Helen/Buck/Eleanor, Helen-Buck/Eleanor/Dan/Joel<br /><br />The ending event was unexpected. I was shocked to read that Buck shot Luke. His own son. Buck is is going to serve time. Luke survives and decides to go to university. He plans to spend a life with Helen. Eleanor completely leaves Buck and even feels sorry for him. What is the most shocking is that due to all the things that the Calder family went through Buck changes. He loses his pride and haughtiness and is devastated. He has lost his wife, lovers, son. Buck has alienated himself from both his family and himself.<br /><br />The best part was the ending paragraph. Three narrow beams of light were shining through the bullet holes of the Hope road sign. The irony was excellent. Probably there is no hope for this place of prejudices and violence against the wolves and people.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11546639631986397225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/359581480?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carinya Kappler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carinya Kappler" href="/user/show/7059901-carinya-kappler">Carinya Kappler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359581480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12674931437898933078">It may be possible, although highly unlikely, for animal loving wild life preservationists to exist harmoniously alongside farmers, hunters and hillbillies. Usually the conflicts of interest experienced by these polarised groups blinds them to the fact that working together is the only way to minimise the damage inflicted by each on the other, and the only way to effect a long term compromise in a successful community. <br/>Nicholas Evans has set his novel in unforgiving terrain harshly afflicted by </span>
  <span id="freeText12674931437898933078" style="display:none">It may be possible, although highly unlikely, for animal loving wild life preservationists to exist harmoniously alongside farmers, hunters and hillbillies. Usually the conflicts of interest experienced by these polarised groups blinds them to the fact that working together is the only way to minimise the damage inflicted by each on the other, and the only way to effect a long term compromise in a successful community. <br />Nicholas Evans has set his novel in unforgiving terrain harshly afflicted by extremes of weather and isolation in and around a small town called “Hope”. To protect the interests of an endangered introduced wolf pack, Government intervention, the scourge of element hardened farmers and small town survivors, arrives in the form of a 29 year old female biologist. Thus ensues a sensitive analysis of an explosive brutal battle between the ranchers and the mild mannered city supporters of an endangered species (the Wolf Pack) exposing the very best and the worst of human nature. <br />It is a moving tale of powerful, self serving bullies weighed down by outrageous outdated chauvinistic attitudes, pitted and disfigured by their own personal losses, betrayals and desperation. The story is emotionally charged, forceful yet with such an overlay of honesty and tenderness that I found it irresistible. <br />“The Horse Whisperer” , Nicholas Evans’ previous novel , rings with similar profound insights into this intriguing minefield of animal and human interaction, understanding and respect.<br />I found parts of “The Loop" brutal, raw and coldly realistic, but felt that the town “Hope” did finally aspire to the promise of its name. <br />Carinya<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer387842815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6932470041793326803">Whenever I go somewhere for my vacation, and wherever that may be, my single most important rule besides bringing my passport and other essentials is: Bring a few promising books.<br/><br/>This summer I went to my aunt's for a few weeks in july. I did bring a few promising books, but none that would satisfy the hastily risen need for a great romance. She and her husband live far up among the Norwegian mountains and I try to visit once a year to get my annual fill of mountain ranges and wilderness - and wh</span>
  <span id="freeText6932470041793326803" style="display:none">Whenever I go somewhere for my vacation, and wherever that may be, my single most important rule besides bringing my passport and other essentials is: Bring a few promising books.<br /><br />This summer I went to my aunt's for a few weeks in july. I did bring a few promising books, but none that would satisfy the hastily risen need for a great romance. She and her husband live far up among the Norwegian mountains and I try to visit once a year to get my annual fill of mountain ranges and wilderness - and while that is wonderful the nearest fab book store is about a two-hour drive away.<br /><br />Instead of shopping, I ransacked her bookshelves and found this novel. It seemed fitting, taking place in a small, remote town called Hope in mid-Montana - like me at the time, situated among mountains. Unfortunately, the read wasn't as enjoyable as I had hoped.<br /><br />While it is very interesting to read about the struggles ranchers have with wildlife; the difficulty of finding a way to balance wildlife and livestock, I felt nothing for the characters (regardless their faction) and that took the pleasure of reading the book away from me. They were far too shallow. I also had expected another kind of love - and epic tale of love combined with a story that dealt with an important and topical discussion, and not getting that was a downer.</span>

    <a title="Henry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10352001-henry"><img alt="Henry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367244190p2/10352001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry" href="/user/show/10352001-henry">Henry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388980732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6423314525818155751">This was a hugely enjoyable read. Nicholas Evans has great insight into the interior workings of both women and men to be convincing when relating their thoughts and experiences. I loved the way he elaborated on the internal personal troubles the characters were dealing with. His thorough research on wolves also made it very captivating for me. <br/>Set in Montana where wolf biologists have to deal with irate farmers when the farmers blame the wolves (sometimes with reason, sometimes not) for losses </span>
  <span id="freeText6423314525818155751" style="display:none">This was a hugely enjoyable read. Nicholas Evans has great insight into the interior workings of both women and men to be convincing when relating their thoughts and experiences. I loved the way he elaborated on the internal personal troubles the characters were dealing with. His thorough research on wolves also made it very captivating for me. <br />Set in Montana where wolf biologists have to deal with irate farmers when the farmers blame the wolves (sometimes with reason, sometimes not) for losses in their stock. Helen Ross is one such wolf lover and biologist who is summoned to mediate and appease in the town of Hope Montana. She also keeps tabs on the wolves and forms a partnership with Luke Calder, the son of one of the most vocal wolf haters, Buck Calder. The story is full of sub plots which makes for interesting reading.<br />This story kept me entertained and had me wondering why this wasn't a best seller like the Evans' "The Horse Whisperer" was. It certainly also has the makings of a beautiful movie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6423314525818155751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uyqyLjbs2/2hgSxVeZ7r3ntHSN0hk/5IfwKDkaHjgDZ6zRed6W1vchRwTE2Nzzxasn7iMXUAU9pNqV4ZP+t0UA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KU3NI3G0KYdrgfcxA0gB1Stv3dBgjb+fDYmwzuNLh0PoqmiQrjWdCN5wlyn3GdZR4lZ3PDQeEg0/Im1GfUNzJQ==')})
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_132274'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/132274.Coast_Road?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Coast Road<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/36492.Barbara_Delinsky?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Barbara Delinsky<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.02 avg rating &mdash; 9,400 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1998\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer18014080480923332551\">Life\'s greatest gifts come to us by accident. Barbara Delinsky has always had a gift for creating tales of extraordinary emotional power and depth. Now the New York Times bestselling author of Three Wishes surpasses herself once again in a novel that<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText18014080480923332551\" style=\"display:none\">Life\'s greatest gifts come to us by accident. Barbara Delinsky has always had a gift for creating tales of extraordinary emotional power and depth. Now the New York Times bestselling author of Three Wishes surpasses herself once again in a novel that takes readers on a journey as richly textured, colorful, and poignant as the northern California landscape in which the book is set. Rachel Keats and Jack McGill were artists, deeply in love when they married, until the rush of life took its toll. After ten years of marriage, they divorced and went their separate ways. Jack stayed in San Francisco. Rachel moved with their two young daughters to Big Sur. Six years later, an alarming middle-of-the-night phone call demands that Jack put aside his own busy life and career as a leading architect to rush to his ex-wife\'s hospital bed. While she lies comatose, Jack maintains a bedside vigil and finds himself getting to know Rachel better than he ever did -- through their daughters, her friends, and, even more, through her art. Meanwhile, the beauty and grace of the Redwood canyon where she has made her home also work their own special alchemy upon Jack. He begins to see Rachel, his daughters, and the story of his marriage with new eyes. Coast Road celebrates those things in life that matter most -- the kinship of neighbors, the companionship of friends, and the irreplaceable time spent with children and family. Avevano quattro gambe, quattro braccia e due volti che permettevano di vedere ovunque. Simili a sfere si muovevano rotolando velocissimi. Erano lisci e levigati, felici e potenti. A causa della loro superbia però furono puniti dagli dèi. E da quel momento non si sono mai più sentiti completi. Hanno iniziato a soffrire e a temere la morte. La storia del pensiero è la storia dei tentativi di porre un rimedio a questa incompletezza, per tornare a essere felici. Di questo, e di nient’altro, hanno parlato i più grandi scrittori greci, fossero poeti come Omero o filosofi come Platone e Aristotele.\nMauro Bonazzi ci accompagna nel labirinto di risposte che gli antichi hanno cercato di dare alla domanda più annosa di tutte: dove si nasconde il senso delle nostre esistenze? Cercare di comprenderlo, attraverso l’aiuto della filosofia, costituisce ancora oggi uno sforzo decisivo per chi è impegnato nel mestiere più bello e difficile, che è quello di vivere bene.\n\n«La civiltà greca ha prodotto una riflessione luminosa sul senso della condizione umana – su quello che siamo e sul valore delle nostre vite – capace di attraversare i secoli, influenzando e stimolando grandi scrittori e grandi pensatori. Lo ha fatto partendo dal tema della morte: questo è il punto di attacco. La morte è uno scandalo, un mistero, qualcosa che non riusciamo e non possiamo accettare. Il problema non è tanto quello di dover morire; ne siamo tutti consapevoli. A essere insopportabile è l’idea che questo fatto, il fatto che prima o poi ce ne andremo, rischia di togliere valore alla nostra esistenza, qui e ora. Quale è il senso di qualcosa che non c’era, c’è e non ci sarà? Quale il valore di qualcosa destinato a scomparire nell’oblio? È questa la domanda a cui bisogna trovare una risposta, perché è qui la chiave per comprendere il senso della nostra esistenza».<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16182208976117885413\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6098.Nicholas_Evans">About Nicholas Evans</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6098.Nicholas_Evans"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1223191539p3/6098.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/6098.Nicholas_Evans">Nicholas Evans
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
897
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10943573088634673267"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i><br/><br/>Nicholas Evans was born and grew up in Worcestershire, England. He studied law at Oxford University, graduating with first class honors, then worked as a journalist for three years on the Evening Chronicle in Newcastle-upon-Tyne. He then moved into televsion, producing films</span>
  <span id="freeText10943573088634673267" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i><br /><br />Nicholas Evans was born and grew up in Worcestershire, England. He studied law at Oxford University, graduating with first class honors, then worked as a journalist for three years on the Evening Chronicle in Newcastle-upon-Tyne. He then moved into televsion, producing films about US politics and the Middle-East for a weekly current affairs programme called Weekend World. It was during this time that he traveled a lot and got to know the United States.<br /><br />In 1982 he started to produce arts documentaries - about famous writers, painters and film-makers, several of which won international awards (films about David Hockney, Francis Bacon, Patricia Highsmith). In 1983 he made a film about the great British director David Lean (Lawrence of Arabia, Doctor Zhivago, etc). Lean became a friend and mentor and persuaded Evans to switch from fact to fiction.<br /><br />For the next ten years, Evans wrote and produced a number of films for television and the cinema. In 1993 he met a blacksmith in the far South-West of England who told him about horse whisperers - people who have the gift of healing traumatized horses. Evans started work on what was to be his first novel.<br /><br />Published in the fall of 1995, The Horse Whisperer has now sold about fifteen million copies across the world. It has been the number one bestseller in about 20 countries and has been translated into 36 languages. It was also made into a movie, starring, produced and directed by Robert Redford.<br /><br />The Loop and The Smoke Jumper, Evans's second and third novels, were again an international bestsellers, topping the bestseller lists in many countries. The Smoke Jumper was published in a paperback edition on July 30, 2003. Evans lives in London and Devon, England.<br /><br /><i>- Nicholas Evans' Website</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10943573088634673267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
